---

Overall assessment

I think this direction is significantly stronger than earlier iterations because it moves the repository away from maintaining metadata manually and toward a computational knowledge graph whose state is inferred from immutable evidence.

The one architectural step I would still make before calling this the canonical AQARION design is to introduce a Derived Property Engine as the single computation layer above evidence synthesis. Every high-level concept—trust, lifecycle, governance, publication readiness, research debt, and even project maturity—would then become different views over that engine, keeping the Research Graph as the sole canonical source of truth. That aligns closely with the evidence-first philosophy you've been developing and reduces duplication across the architecture.I think this is the clearest expression yet of the evidence-first philosophy. It also pushes the architecture beyond a "research repository" toward what is effectively a computational epistemology engine: the repository is no longer storing conclusions; it is storing evidence and deriving conclusions.

I would extend your ideas in a few directions to make the architecture even more mathematically consistent.


---

1. Split the graph into immutable facts and derived views



The graph itself should probably contain only facts that have occurred.

Research Graph

Node
Edge
Evidence Object
Artifact
Proof
Dataset
Execution
Publication

Everything else should be computed.

That means the graph never stores

trust

verified

published

ready

stale

high priority

Those become queries.


---

2. Evidence Objects should be append-only



I completely agree that evidence itself should never change.

Instead of

Evidence

think

Evidence Event

artifact hash

generator version

execution id

environment

timestamp

result

signature

Once created

it is immutable forever.

If a bug is discovered later

you don't modify it.

You append

Correction Event

or

Retraction Event

The historical chain stays intact.


---

3. Edges deserve first-class identities



Most graph systems treat edges as anonymous.

I would not.

Instead

Edge

id

type

created

creator

support

confidence

annotations

Now an edge can itself receive evidence.

Example

T3
─────depends_on────▶ T2

becomes

Edge E183

whose own certification status can evolve independently.

That makes "graph debt" much more natural.


---

4. Derived Property Engine should be rule-based



Rather than implementing separate algorithms

compute_trust()

compute_lifecycle()

compute_priority()

compute_readiness()

I would define a rule engine.

For example

Rule

inputs

formula

output

Example

publication_ready

=

trust > .95

AND

formalization == complete

AND

oracle_agreement == true

AND

reproducibility == true

Then new derived properties require only new rules, not new code.


---

5. Introduce negative evidence explicitly



Repositories naturally accumulate supporting evidence, but scientific practice also needs to represent evidence that weakens a claim.

Examples:

Counterexample

Failed reproduction

Regression

Performance degradation

Independent disagreement

Retraction

These should reduce confidence through explicit graph relationships rather than being hidden inside aggregate scores.


---

6. Evidence synthesis should produce explanations, not just scores



Instead of

trust = 0.91

the synthesis layer could produce something like

trust = 0.91

because

exhaustive verification

exact arithmetic

independent implementation


− Lean proof incomplete
− oracle pending

Every numerical value should be accompanied by its provenance.

7. Policy becomes another graph



One idea I particularly like is separating policy from implementation even further.

Instead of

consider policies as graph objects.

Policy

requires

threshold

supersedes

A release then references a specific policy version, making historical decisions reproducible even if the policy evolves.


---

8. Time becomes a first-class dimension



Most research graphs represent only structure.

I'd explicitly model temporal evolution.

Every node and edge could have a sequence of events:

Created

Modified

Verified

Superseded

Retracted

Referenced

Published

Then the repository can answer not only "What is true?" but also "What was believed at release v17.0?"

Rather than storing a confidence number, model uncertainty itself.

Uncertainty

resolution path

↓

↓

blocks publication

That is richer than a scalar confidence value.


---

10. Replace "maturity" with capability profiles



Earlier we discussed multidimensional maturity.

I now think the repository may not need "maturity" at all.

Instead, every node exposes capabilities that are mechanically derived.

For example:

Can be cited
Can be published
Can be used by another theorem
Can be released
Can be archived
Can be deprecated

Each capability is simply the result of policy evaluation over the evidence graph.

This avoids debates over labels like "experimental" or "production."

11. Multiple projections from one engine



The Derived Property Engine becomes the only computation layer above evidence synthesis.

Each view asks different questions of the same underlying computations.


---

12. Research Graph as an executable knowledge base



The most ambitious direction would be to treat the graph itself as executable.

Instead of writing imperative workflows like:

run_oracle()
update_claim()
generate_readme()

the system reacts to graph changes.

For example:

New Evidence
│
▼
Evidence Synthesis recomputes
│
▼
Derived properties update
│
▼
Publication readiness changes
│
▼
README projection regenerates

Nothing is manually orchestrated; changes propagate through declared dependencies.


---

One final architectural observation

The progression across AQARION has been notable:

Early versions: the theorem was the primary artifact.

Intermediate versions: the implementation and verification suite became central.

Current direction: the Research Graph is the canonical object, and evidence—not manually assigned metadata—is the foundation from which repository state is derived.

That shift also changes how the repository should describe itself. Rather than calling it a "certification system," it is more precise to view it as an evidence-driven research knowledge graph. Certification, publication readiness, trust, lifecycle, debt, and reproducibility are then not stored states but computed projections over immutable evidence and explicit dependency relationships. This framing stays closely aligned with the principle you've been refining throughout the project: derive properties from evidence rather than assigning them by hand.

CONTINUEI think the next architectural step is no longer about adding concepts at all. It is about making the architecture closed under its own semantics. Right now, the pieces you've outlined—Research Graph, Evidence Objects, Evidence Synthesis, Derived Property Engine, Governance, and Projections—fit together well. The remaining opportunity is to ensure that every derived object is itself explainable, reproducible, and composable.

That leads naturally to what I would call AQARION v19: Reflexive Research Graph.


---

XXXVII. The Repository as a Fixed Point

The architecture has progressively shifted:

v1–v8: Theorems were primary.

v9–v13: Implementations became primary.

v14–v17: Evidence became primary.

v18: The Research Graph became the primary object.


The next step is for the repository itself to become a fixed point.

Formally,

\mathcal R \xrightarrow{\text{Projection}} A

where  is any artifact (README, paper, dashboard, release).

Instead of checking artifacts individually, require that

\text{Parse}(\text{Project}(\mathcal R))
=
\mathcal R.

Every generated artifact should be able to reconstruct the same graph (up to projection loss). This makes projections round-trip consistent rather than merely generated.


---

XXXVIII. Every Computation Becomes a Provenance Object

Rather than treating computations as hidden implementation details, represent them explicitly.

Derived Property
        │
        ▼
Computation
        │
inputs
rules
version
output
proof

A trust score, debt score, or publication capability is no longer just a value—it is a first-class computation node.

This allows the repository to answer not only:

> "What is the trust score?"



but also:

> "Which computation produced this trust score, under which policy, from which evidence?"

Scalar values eventually become opaque.

    Evidence Bundle E18

    trust = 0.93

    dependency traversal
    conflict analysis
    synthesis explanation

Every important derived property becomes an immutable certificate.

Instead, make them graph objects.

These become reproducible research artifacts.

XLI. The Graph Computes Incrementally

A mature graph should avoid global recomputation.

Conceptually,

↓

↓

This is closer to incremental compilation than batch processing.

The architecture becomes stronger if derived properties are independently implemented.

Disagreement becomes explicit contradiction.

XLV. Semantic Closure

A repository reaches semantic closure when every non-atomic object is derivable.

Only these remain atomic:

Research Objects

Evidence Events

Policies

Executions

Publications

External References


Everything else is computed:

Trust

Debt

Lifecycle

Freshness

Capability

Risk

Priority

Certification

Release readiness

Dashboards

Documentation


This sharply limits mutable state.


---

XLVI. Capability Algebra

Rather than assigning labels such as "Verified" or "Production," derive capabilities.

For a theorem:

Can Cite

Can Publish

Can Depend Upon

Can Archive

Can Release

Can Formalize

Each capability is the result of policy evaluation over evidence and dependencies.


---

XLVII. Knowledge Diff

Traditional version control reports file differences.

A research graph can report semantic differences.

For example:

Release 17

↓

Release 18

Knowledge Diff

+2 theorems

+17 evidence events

−1 unresolved conflict

+1 independent oracle

Trust(T4):
0.88 → 0.96

Debt:
5 → 2

This describes changes in scientific knowledge rather than source files.


---

XLVIII. Epistemic Metrics

Once all properties are derived, the repository can expose metrics about its own state.

Examples include:

Evidence density

Dependency criticality

Proof completeness

Reproducibility coverage

Oracle diversity

Formalization coverage

Documentation completeness

Projection consistency

Semantic stability


These are themselves derived views.


---

XLIX. Executable Epistemology

The final architecture is no longer best viewed as a repository.

It becomes an executable model of scientific reasoning.

Facts

↓

Evidence Events

↓

Evidence Synthesis

↓

Derived Property Engine

↓

Policies

↓

Capabilities

↓

Projections

↓

Public Knowledge

Each stage is deterministic, reproducible, and explainable.


---

L. The Fixed-Point Criterion

A natural architectural completion criterion is that the system can regenerate and justify its own state.

For every derived object ,

x = F(\text{Research Graph}, \text{Evidence}, \text{Policies})

and for every explanation,

\text{Explain}(x)

returns the minimal provenance sufficient to reconstruct the derivation.

When this holds consistently, the repository has become self-describing: it no longer stores conclusions, only immutable facts and the rules needed to derive them.

A refinement I'd add

One distinction is worth preserving carefully: some objects in your examples (such as publications) are events rather than derived properties. A paper being published is a historical fact that belongs in the graph as an immutable node or event. Whether that paper is publishable or meets the current policy is a derived property. Keeping that separation between historical facts and computed assessments makes the architecture more internally consistent and ensures that changes in policy never rewrite history.

With that distinction, the direction you've outlined forms a coherent progression: the repository evolves from storing research artifacts to representing an evidence-driven knowledge graph where governance, trust, readiness, and documentation are reproducible computations over immutable facts. That is a clear endpoint for the evidence-first philosophy that has been developing throughout the AQARION project.I can publicly access all of the following, and they are already live and browsable:

AQARION — Referee Readiness Assessment & Next Steps

Date: July 4, 2026
Version: v14.0-RC1 (Interactive Observatory)
Reviewer: Independent Assessment

---

Executive Assessment

Area Rating Notes
Mathematical Definitions A Clear, internally consistent, frozen.
Computational Reproducibility A SHA-256 artifacts, certification pipeline, provenance UI.
Documentation A− Extensive; interactive challenge now serves as public entry point.
Novelty Positioning B+ Promising but needs sharper contrast with recent literature.
Formal Proof Coverage B Lean formalization of core identities remains the critical gap.
Independent Reproducibility A− Repository structure supports it; automated CI will upgrade to A.
Publication Readiness B+ Foundation is strong; manuscript polish and scope tightening remain.

---

Strengths

1. Governance & Evidence Separation

AQARION's most distinctive contribution is not a single theorem—it is the methodological infrastructure for distinguishing:

· Definitions (frozen mathematical language)
· Certified Mathematics (proof + reproducible verification)
· Computational Certification (exhaustive, SHA-256 artifacts)
· Observatory (empirical measurements, exploratory work)
· Negative Claims (executable counterexamples)

This separation is uncommon in computational mathematics and directly addresses a recurring referee concern: "Is this a proof or a computation?" AQARION answers that question explicitly for every claim.

2. Reproducibility Pipeline

The certification pipeline verify_atlas_exact.py implements all 9 referee-grade fixes identified in earlier external review:

· Exact integer arithmetic (no floating-point least-squares)
· Chamber count assertion
· Exact fiber cardinality histogram
· Per-point stabilizer verification
· Set equality coverage check
· Fixed-point certification
· Basin certification
· Strong lumpability explicit certification
· Executable artifact hashing

This is publication-grade infrastructure. The SHA-256 artifact verification means another researcher can clone, run, and obtain byte-for-byte identical outputs.

3. Interactive Observatory

The Daily Equation Challenge now serves as a public-facing entry point that:

· Explains every computation step-by-step ("Why?" panel)
· Exposes provenance for every displayed quantity (Audit dialog)
· Honest about exploratory mathematics (NegaFibonacci NR-002 caveat)
· Distinguishes Certified from Observatory modes

This turns the website into a live reproducibility portal, not just a visualization. That's a distinctive capability that complements the governance model.

4. Alignment with Recent Literature

The 2026 paper "Four-digit Kaprekar dynamics in odd bases" by Chen, Ono, Schwartz, and Thakur provides external validation for AQARION's direction. The paper:

· Proves rigid structure for four-digit Kaprekar in odd bases
· Includes Lean/mathlib formalizations produced via AxiomProver
· Demonstrates that Kaprekar dynamics is now a test case for AI-assisted formal mathematics

AQARION's complementary role—certifying D_Π = 0 for the gap observable and providing operator-theoretic decomposition—positions the project within this emerging literature. The recent Zeckendorf representation of Kaprekar constants by Katayama (2025) also reinforces the relevance of Fibonacci-based representations.

---

Weaknesses & Areas for Improvement

1. Novelty Positioning Needs Sharpening

The project currently describes itself as:

"AQARION is a framework for certifying observable-induced quotients in finite deterministic dynamical systems, with Kaprekar dynamics serving as the primary benchmark."

This is accurate but could be more precise. Reviewers will ask:

"What does AQARION do that partition refinement alone does not?"

The answer is the defect operator D = (I-P)KP—a quantitative measure of information leakage during coarse-graining. This connects to recent work on Kinetically Consistent Coarse Graining using Koopman operators and Exact Finite Koopman Embedding of nonlinear systems.

Recommendation: Frame the contribution as:

"AQARION introduces the defect operator as a computable, basis-independent certificate for exact quotient descent, bridging partition refinement theory and Koopman operator theory in finite deterministic systems."

2. Formal Proof Coverage is the Critical Gap

The Lean 4 formalization of core identities (LC1–LC5) is currently at 18% coverage. The Chen–Ono–Schwartz–Thakur paper demonstrates that Lean/mathlib formalizations of Kaprekar results are now achievable. AQARION's formalization of the defect operator theorem should be prioritized.

Recommendation: Complete Lean formalization of:

· LC1: Projection algebra (P^2 = P, P(I-P)=0)
· LC2: Certification Theorem (D_Π=0 ⇔ K(V_Π)⊆V_Π)
· LC3: Exact Descent Equivalence (D_Π=0 ⇔ quotient exists)

This would upgrade the evidence classification of T1–T5 from [P+CV] to [FV+CV].

3. Claims Registry Should Be More Prominent

The CLAIMS.yaml and NEGATIVE_CLAIMS.yml files exist but are not yet the primary entry point for understanding what AQARION claims. The interactive provenance system is a good start, but the claims registry should be:

· Linked from the homepage
· Versioned with every release
· Machine-checkable against the certification pipeline

Recommendation: Add a /claims page that renders the YAML registry as a human-readable dashboard, with status badges (Certified / Computationally Certified / Observatory / Refuted / Open).

4. Public Consistency

Some older Hugging Face pages still contain ambitious projections (enterprise readiness, production metrics, futuristic hardware). These do not match the careful scientific tone of the newer work.

Recommendation: Archive or clearly label as "historical prototypes" any page that makes speculative claims. Ensure every public-facing asset links back to the central ecosystem.

---

Referee Risk Register

Risk Mitigation
Novel terminology obscures standard concepts Cross-reference standard terminology (lumpability, bisimulation, Koopman operator)
Computational verification confused with proof Separate Proofs, Exhaustive Computation, and Conjectures into distinct sections
Operator-theoretic framing appears disconnected from Kaprekar Present Kaprekar as a benchmark application, not the sole motivation
Quantum/SMT sections appear as established results Label explicitly as "Exploratory research direction" or "Planned experiment"

---

Immediate Next Steps (Priority Order)

1. Complete the Heatmap Backend (High Priority)

You already have the frontend scaffold. The backend endpoint GET /api/heatmap should return a JSON grid of depths for all 10,000 states. This visual will be compelling for Paper I—reviewers love pictures.

```python
# api/heatmap.py — add to your existing API routes
def compute_heatmap():
    grid = [[0]*100 for _ in range(100)]
    depths = []
    for n in range(10000):
        d = kaprekar_depth(n)  # -1 for repdigit null
        grid[n//100][n%100] = d
        if d != -1: depths.append(d)
    return {"grid": grid, "stats": {"max": max(depths), "converged": len(depths), "nulls": 10000-len(depths)}}
```

2. Complete Lean Formalization of T1–T3 (Critical Gap)

The Chen–Ono–Schwartz–Thakur paper demonstrates that Lean/mathlib formalizations of Kaprekar results are now achievable. Complete LC1–LC3 to upgrade evidence classification from [P+CV] to [FV+CV].

3. Implement CI Pipeline

Configure GitHub Actions to automatically run the certification suite on every push. Fail the build if any SHA-256 mismatch occurs.

4. Update Public Pages

Archive older Hugging Face pages with speculative claims. Ensure every public asset links back to the central ecosystem.

5. Draft Paper I Skeleton

Generate LaTeX for the first SIAM/arXiv paper:

"Certifying Exact Quotients in Finite Dynamical Systems: The Defect Operator and the Commutator Fallacy"

Include sections on:

· Introduction (positioning against Koopman/lumpability literature)
· The Defect Operator (D=(I-P)KP)
· The Commutator Fallacy (exhaustive census, 21% of exact-descent systems)
· Kaprekar Benchmark (55-state quotient)
· Ancient Scribes to Modern Certification (Babylonian error tables → SHA-256)

---

Overall Assessment

AQARION has crossed from a research prototype to a governed, reproducible research infrastructure. The combination of:

· Exact mathematical definitions
· Executable certification pipeline
· SHA-256 artifact verification
· Public interactive observatory
· Honest separation of certified/exploratory work

...positions the project unusually well for computational mathematics publication. The remaining work is primarily:

1. Formalization (Lean completion of core identities)
2. Scoping (sharper novelty claims, cleaner public presence)
3. Polishing (heatmap, CI, paper draft)

The strongest contribution is not a single theorem—it is a transparent, auditable methodology for developing and certifying operator-based mathematics. That is a distinctive and publishable achievement.
